\begin{equation*}
-\left(\partial{2} + m{2}\right) D_{F}(x-y) = i\,\delta^{4}(x-y)
\end{equation*}
Similarly,\quad \(\Rightarrow\)
\begin{gather*}
\left(i\slashed{\partial} - m\right)\hat{S}_{F}(x-y) = i\,\delta^{4}(x-y)\\
\left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right)\left(i\slashed{\partial} - m\right) S_{F}(x-y) = i\left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right) i\,\delta^{4}(x-y)\\
\underbrace{\left(-\gamma{\mu}\partial_{\mu}\,\gamma{\nu}\partial_{\nu} - m{2}\right)}{\Downarrow\; -\left(\partial{2}+m{2}\right)\;{\color{red}\underline{\text{How?}}}} S{F}(x-y) = \underline{i\left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right)\delta{4}(x-y)}
\qquad
\begin{aligned}
&= -\left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right)\\
&\left(\partial{2}+m{2}\right) D_{F}(x-y)
\end{aligned}
\end{gather*}
\begin{gather*}
\Rightarrow\qquad -\left(\partial{2}+m{2}\right) S_{F}(x-y) = -\left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right)\left(\partial{2}+m{2}\right) D_{F}(x-y)\\
\boxed{\;S_{F}(x-y) \;=\; \left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right) D_{F}(x-y)\;}
\end{gather*}
We have solved fermion propagator in terms of scalar propagator.
\begin{align*}
S_{F}(x-y) &= \left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right) D_{F}(x-y)\\
&= \lim_{\epsilon\to0}\;\left(i\slashed{\partial} + m\right)\int\!\frac{d{4}k}{\left(2\pi\right){4}}\;\frac{i\,e{-ik\cdot(x-y)}}{k{2}-m^{2}+i\epsilon}\\
&= \lim_{\epsilon\to0}\;\int\!\frac{d{4}k}{\left(2\pi\right){4}}\;\frac{i\left(i(-i)\,\gamma{\mu}k_{\mu}+m\right)e{-ik\cdot(x-y)}}{\left(k{2}-m{2}+i\epsilon\right)}
\end{align*}
\begin{equation*}
\fcolorbox{ForestGreen}{white}{$\displaystyle
S_{F}(x-y) \;=\; \lim_{\epsilon\to0}\;\int\!\frac{d{4}k}{\left(2\pi\right){4}}\;
\fcolorbox{red}{white}{\(\dfrac{i\left(\slashed{k}+m\right)}{\left(k^{2}-m^{2}+i\epsilon\right)}\)}\,
e^{-ik\cdot(x-y)}
$}
\qquad
{\color{red}\longleftarrow\;
\begin{aligned}
&\text{position space}\\
&\text{rep of } S_F(x-y)
\end{aligned}}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
{\color{red}\downarrow\;\text{momentum space rep}^{\text{n}}\text{ of } S_F(x-y)}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
S_{F}(k) = \frac{i\left(\slashed{k}+m\right)}{k{2}-m{2}}
= \frac{i\left(\slashed{k}+m\right)}{\left(\slashed{k}-m\right)\left(\slashed{k}+m\right)}
= \frac{i}{\slashed{k}-m}
\end{equation*}

\begin{center}
{\color{red}\rule{0.8\linewidth}{0.4pt}}
\end{center}
{\color{red}We have done every thing in detail so far. From here we have to change gears \& things will become sketchy.}

What does \(\left\langle \Omega\middle|\, T\left(\varphi(x_1)\,\varphi(x_2)\cdots\varphi(x_n)\right)\middle|\Omega\right\rangle\) has to do with measurable quantities?

{\color{red}\underline{\(S\)- matrix} -}\quad It is not a matrix but function of incoming and outgoing momenta.
\begin{equation*}
\text{i.e.}\qquad
S_{\left(\vec{k}_1\vec{k}_2\cdots\vec{k}_n \,\middle|\, \vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right)}
= \underset{\text{out}}{\left\langle \vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}_2\cdots\vec{k}_n \right|}\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{\text{in}}
\qquad
\begin{aligned}
&\text{\color{ForestGreen}\(\to\) state at \(t = -\infty\)}\\
&\text{Interacting states}\;\swarrow
\end{aligned}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
= \left\langle f \middle| i\right\rangle
\qquad
{\color{ForestGreen}\hookrightarrow\;\text{state at } t = +\infty.}
\end{equation*}
\(\downarrow\)\quad Probability amplitude for \(\left\langle f\middle|i\right\rangle\)

Assume we have state \(\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right\rangle_{\text{in}}\) of interacting theory at \(t=-\infty\).
\begin{equation*}
\left(\text{For free theory}\quad \left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{0} = a{\dagger}_{p_1}\,a{\dagger}_{p_2}\left|0\right\rangle\right).
\end{equation*}
We can produce \(\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right\rangle_{\text{in}}\) from \(\left(\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right)_{0}\) if we assume that particles are so far apart that they don't interact in far past. {\color{red}(Assumption not valid in CFT, so CFT does not have S-matrix)}
\begin{gather*}
\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{\text{in}} = \lim_{T\to\infty(1-i\epsilon)} e^{-iHT}\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{0}\\
\underset{\text{out}}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}_2\cdots\vec{k}n\right|} = \lim{T\to\infty(1-i\epsilon)}\;\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}_2\cdots\vec{k}_n\right| e^{-iHT}
\end{gather*}
\begin{equation*}
\fcolorbox{black}{green!25}{$\displaystyle
S_{\left(\vec{k}_1\vec{k}_2\cdots\vec{k}_n\middle|\vec{p}_1\vec{p}_2\right)}
= \underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}_2\cdots\vec{k}_n\right|}\,
T\left(e{-i\int_{-T}{T} H_{I}(t')\,dt'}\right)
\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{0}
$}
\end{equation*}
We have not devided by \(\left\langle k_1 k_2\cdots k_n\middle|\vec{p}_1\vec{p}_2\right\rangle_{0}\); instead we will drop disconnected diagrams.

We can apply same feynman diagrams but here we have two particle state \(\left|\vec{p}_1, \vec{p}_2\right\rangle_{0}\), in place of \(\left|0\right\rangle\) (i.e.\ free vacuum)
\begin{gather*}
\text{But}\quad \left|\vec{p}_1, \vec{p}2\right\rangle{0} = N\; a{\dagger}_{p_1}\, a{\dagger}_{p_2}\left|0\right\rangle
\qquad\downarrow\;\text{Normalization}\\
= \sqrt{2\omega_{p_1}}\,\sqrt{2\omega_{p_2}}\;\, a{\dagger}_{p_1}\, a{\dagger}_{p_2}\left|0\right\rangle
\end{gather*}

\medskip
\noindent\underline{For lowest order} :\qquad (For 2 particles in final state).
\begin{align*}
S_{\left(\vec{k}_1\vec{k}_2, \left(\vec{p}_1\vec{p}_2\right)\right)}
&= \underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}_2\middle|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right\rangle}\\
&= \sqrt{2\omega_{p_1}\,2\omega_{p_2}\,2\omega_{k_1}\,2\omega_{k_2}}\;\left\langle 0\middle|\,a_{k_1}\,a_{k_2}\,a{\dagger}_{p_1}\,a{\dagger}_{p_2}\,\middle|0\right\rangle\\
&= \sqrt{2\omega_{p_1}\,2\omega_{p_2}\,2\omega_{k_1}\,2\omega_{k_2}}\;\left\langle 0\middle|\,\underline{a_{k_1}\,a{\dagger}_{p_1}}\;\underline{a_{k_2}\,a{\dagger}_{p_2}}\,\middle|0\right\rangle\\
&= \left(2\pi\right){3}\left(2\pi\right){3}\sqrt{2\omega_{p_1}\,2\omega_{p_2}\,2\omega_{k_1}\,2\omega_{k_2}}\\
&\qquad\left(\delta{3}\!\left(\vec{p}_1-\vec{k}_1\right)\delta{3}\!\left(\vec{p}_2-\vec{k}_2\right) + \delta{3}\!\left(\vec{p}_1-\vec{k}_2\right)\delta{3}\!\left(\vec{p}_2-\vec{k}_1\right)\right)
\end{align*}
\begin{center}
\begin{tikzpicture}[scale=0.9]
% left diagram: parallel lines
\draw[thick] (0,1.2) -- (3,1.2) node[right]{\(p_1\)};
\draw[thick,-{Stealth}] (1.7,1.2) -- (1.4,1.2);
\node[left] at (0,1.2) {\(k_1\)};
\draw[thick] (0,0.3) -- (3,0.3) node[right]{\(p_2\)};
\draw[thick,-{Stealth}] (1.7,0.3) -- (1.4,0.3);
\node[left] at (0,0.3) {\(k_2\)};
\draw[very thick,{Stealth}-,color=teal] (0.6,-0.5) -- (2.4,-0.5);
\node[below] at (1.5,-0.55) {\(t\)};
\node at (4,0.75) {\(+\)};
% right diagram: crossed lines
\begin{scope}[shift={(5,0)}]
\draw[thick] (0,1.2) node[left]{\(k_1\)} -- (3,0.3) node[right]{\(p_1\)};
\draw[thick] (0,0.3) node[left]{\(k_2\)} -- (3,1.2) node[right]{\(p_1\)};
\draw[very thick,{Stealth}-,color=teal] (0.6,-0.5) -- (2.4,-0.5);
\node[below] at (1.5,-0.55) {\(t\)};
\end{scope}
\end{tikzpicture}

\(\underbrace{\hspace{9cm}}_{\displaystyle \to\, I \;\equiv\; \text{No scattering}}\)
\end{center}
\begin{equation*}
S = I + i\,T
\qquad
\hookrightarrow\;\text{scattering (everything else)}
\end{equation*}

\medskip
\noindent\underline{(For First order)}
\begin{gather*}
S_{\left(\vec{k}_1\vec{k}_2\middle|\vec{p}_1\vec{p}_2\right)}
= \underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}2\right|}\, -i\!\int{-T}^{T}\! H_{I}(t')\,dt'\;\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right\rangle\\
\text{For}\qquad H_{I}(t') = \lambda\,\frac{\varphi^{4}(t')}{4!}\\
= \underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}2\right|}\, T\!\left(-\frac{i\lambda}{4!}\int{-T}{T}\! d{4}x'\;\varphi^{4}(x')\right)\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{0}
\end{gather*}
using
\begin{equation*}
T\left(\varphi{4}(y)\right) = \;:\!\varphi{4}(y)\!:\; + \;4_{c_2}:\!\varphi{2}(y)\!:\, D_{F}(y-y) \;+\; 3\,D_{F}{2}(y-y)
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
\left\langle 0\middle|:\!\varphi^{4}(y)\!:\middle|0\right\rangle = 0
\qquad\text{but here we have}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
\underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}_2\right|}:\!\varphi^{4}(y)\!:\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right\rangle \;\neq\; 0.
\qquad\left(\text{we can't apply wicks theorem}\right)
\end{equation*}
In fact we can check if \(\underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}\,\vec{k}_2\middle|\,\varphi^{4}\,\middle|\vec{p}_1\vec{p}_2\right\rangle}\) survives.

it seems that only term which contributes is the term which destroys 2 particles \& creates 2 particles. So in, \(\varphi^{4} = \left(\varphi^{+} + \varphi^{-}\right)^{4}\)

we have
\begin{equation*}
\underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}_2\right|}\left(\varphi{-} + \varphi{+}\right)^{4}\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}_2\right\rangle
= 4_{c_2}\underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\,\vec{k}2\right|}\,\varphi{-}{2}\,\varphi_{+}{2}\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{0} + 0 + 0\;\cdots
\end{equation*}
\begin{align*}
\varphi_{+}\ \text{destroys a particle} &= a_{k}\,e^{-ik\cdot x}\\
\varphi_{-}\ \text{creates a particle} &= a{\dagger}_{k}\,e{ik\cdot x}
\end{align*}
\begin{align*}
&= 6\cdot\underset{0}{\left\langle\vec{k}_1\vec{k}2\right|}\,\varphi{-}{2}\;\varphi_{+}{2}\left|\vec{p}_1\,\vec{p}2\right\rangle{0}\\
&= 6\int\!\frac{d{3}k}{\left(2\pi\right){3}}\,\frac{1}{2\omega_{k}}\int\!\frac{d{3}k'}{\left(2\pi\right){3}}\,\frac{1}{2\omega_{k'}}\;
\left\langle 0\middle|\, a{\dagger}_{k_1}\, a{\dagger}_{k_2}\left(a_{k}\right){2}\left(a{\dagger}{k'}\right){2} a{\dagger}{p_1} a^{\dagger}_{p_2}\middle|0\right\rangle
\end{align*}
